المطلب الثاني : الاعتراض عليه بنقل الخلاف
وذلك أن يستدل مدع على حكم مسألة بقول صحابي، أو عدد من الصحابة باعتباره دليلا شرعيّا فيواجهه المخالف بنقل رأي مخالف لصحابي آخر أو عدد من الصحابة الآخرين مخالفين في قولهم قول الصحابة المحتج بقولهم، ومثاله، استدلال المالكي على أن العِدَّتين لا تتداخلان لما روي عن عمر وعلي رضي الله عنهما أنهما قالا تعتد من الأول بقية العدة ثم تستقبل العدة من الثاني، فيقول الحنفي : قد روي عن معاذ بن جبل مثل قولنا فصارت المسألة خلافا بينهم، والجواب : أن يتكلم المستدل على المنقول عن معاذ بما يسقطه ليسلم له قول عمر وعلي رضي الله عنهما ومثاله كذلك : احتجاج الجمهور غير المالكية بعمل علي وقوله على أن الرجل إذا عقد على امرأة معتدة من زواج سابق ودخل بها فإنه يفرق بينهما لكنها لا تحرم عليه على سبيل التأبيد، قال الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله : أخبرنا عبد المجيد عن ابن جريج قال أخبرنا عطاء أن رجلا طلق امرأته، فاعتدت منه حتى إذا بقي شيء من عدتها نكحها رجل في آخر عدتها – جهلا وبنى بها، فأتي علي بن أبي طالب رضي الله عنه في ذلك، ففرق بينهما، وأمرها أن تعتد ما بقي من عدتها الأولى ثم تعتد من هذا عدة مستقبلة، فإذا انقضت عدتها فهي بالخيار إن شاءت نكحت وإن شاءت فلا فيعترض عليهم المالكية بما نُقل عن عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه أنه حكم بتأبيد تحريمها عليه فقد روى مالك في الموطأ عن ابن شهاب الزهري عن سعيد بن المسيب وسليمان بن يسار أن عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه فرق بين طليحة الأسدية وزوجها رشيد الثقفي لما تزوجها في العدة من شخص آخر، وقال: «أيما امرأة نكحت في عدتها فإن كان زوجها الذي تزوجها لم يدخل بها فرق بينهما ثم اعتدت بقية عدتها من الأول ثم كان الآخر خاطبًا من الخطاب، وإن كان دخل بها فرق بينهما ثم اعتدت بقية عدتها من الأول ثم اعتدت من الآخر، ثم لا يجتمعان أبداء وقد أجاب الجمهور على هذا الاعتراض بأنه ثبت رجوع عمر رضي الله عنه إلى قول علي رضي الله عنه، وذلك في الحادثة المذكورة نفسها، فقد روي أن امرأة من قريش قد تزوجها رجل من ثقيف في عدتها، فلما بلغ عمر ذلك أرسل إليهما ففرق بينهما وعاقبهما، وقال: لا ينكحها أبدا، وجعل الصداق في بيت المال، وفشا ذلك بين الناس، فبلغ عليا، فقال: «رحم الله أمير المؤمنين، ما بال الصداق وبيت المال ؛ إنهما جهلا فينبغي للإمام أن يردهما إلى السنة»؛ قيل : فما تقول أنت فيهما ؟ قال : «لها الصداق بما استحل من فرجها ويفرق بينهما ولا جلد عليهما وتكمل عدتها من الأول، ثم تكمل العدة من الآخر، ثم يكون خاطبًا»، فقال: «أيها الناس ردوا الجهالات إلى السنة» فبلغ ذلك عمر، فقال: «أيها الناس ردوا الجهالات إلى السنة»
The Second Demand: Objection by Citing Disagreement
That is: a claimant infers the ruling of a case by the saying of a Companion, or a number of Companions, considering it a legal proof. Then the opponent confronts him by citing a conflicting opinion of another Companion or a number of other Companions whose saying contradicts the saying of the Companions cited as proof. An example: the Maliki argues that the two waiting periods do not overlap based on what was narrated from Umar and Ali, may Allah be pleased with them, that they said: 'She waits the remainder of the first waiting period, then she begins the waiting period from the second [marriage].' The Hanafi says: 'It has been narrated from Muadh ibn Jabal something like our view, so the matter becomes a disagreement among them.' The answer: the proponent must discuss what was narrated from Muadh in a way that nullifies it so that the saying of Umar and Ali, may Allah be pleased with them, remains valid for him. Another example: the argument of the non-Maliki majority by the act and saying of Ali that if a man contracts marriage with a woman who is in the waiting period from a previous marriage and consummates it, they are separated but she does not become permanently forbidden to him. Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'Abd al-Majid narrated to us from Ibn Jurayj who said: Ata narrated to us that a man divorced his wife, and she observed the waiting period until when there remained something of her waiting period, a man married her in the last part of her waiting period – out of ignorance – and consummated the marriage. Then Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, was approached concerning that. He separated them and ordered her to complete what remained of her first waiting period, then observe a new waiting period from this [second] marriage. When her waiting period ends, she has the choice: if she wishes she may marry [him], and if she wishes she may not.' The Malikis object to them by what was narrated from Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, that he ruled the permanent prohibition of her to him. Malik narrated in al-Muwatta from Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and Sulayman ibn Yasar that Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, separated between Tulayha al-Asadiyya and her husband Rashid al-Thaqafi when he married her during the waiting period from another person, and said: 'Any woman who marries during her waiting period – if the husband who married her has not consummated, they are separated, then she completes the remainder of her waiting period from the first [husband], then the other becomes one of the suitors. If he has consummated, they are separated, then she completes the remainder of her waiting period from the first, then she observes a waiting period from the other, then they never come together again.' The majority answered this objection by stating that Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, retracted to the saying of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, in the very same incident. For it was narrated that a woman from Quraysh was married by a man from Thaqif during her waiting period. When Umar learned of that, he sent for them, separated them, punished them, and said: 'He shall never marry her,' and put the dowry in the public treasury. This spread among the people and reached Ali, who said: 'May Allah have mercy on the Commander of the Faithful. What is the matter with the dowry and the public treasury? They were ignorant. The Imam should bring them back to the Sunnah.' It was said: 'What do you say about them?' He said: 'She has the dowry for what he made lawful of her private parts. They are separated, no flogging upon them. She completes her waiting period from the first, then completes the waiting period from the other, then he becomes a suitor.' Then he said: 'O people, return the ignorances to the Sunnah.' That reached Umar, who said: 'O people, return the ignorances to the Sunnah.'
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage describes a specific type of objection (اعتراض) in dialectical debate (jadal): objecting by citing disagreement among the Companions (نقل الخلاف). The author explains the method: when a debater (المستدل) uses a Companion's saying as a legal proof (دليل شرعي), the opponent (المخالف) can counter by citing a different Companion's saying that contradicts the first. This turns the matter into a disagreement among the Companions, thereby neutralizing the original proof. The required answer (الجواب) is that the proponent must discuss the opposing narration in a way that nullifies it (يسقطه), so that his original Companion evidence remains valid. Two examples illustrate the point. First, the Maliki cites Umar and Ali on non-overlapping waiting periods (عدتين لا تتداخلان); the Hanafi responds by citing Muadh ibn Jabal with the opposite view. The Maliki must then discredit Muadh's narration. Second, the majority (non-Malikis) rely on Ali's ruling that a marriage during iddah does not cause permanent prohibition. The Malikis object by citing Umar's ruling of permanent prohibition in the case of Tulayha al-Asadiyya. The answer is that Umar later retracted to Ali's position in a similar incident, as shown by the detailed narration where Umar initially ruled harshly but upon hearing Ali's reasoning, he publicly announced the same correction: 'ردوا الجهالات إلى السنة'. Thus, the objection is answered by proving the opposing authority's earlier opinion was later abandoned. The passage demonstrates the practical application of this jadal technique.

Key Terms
الاعتراض بنقل الخلاف
قول الصحابي
الجواب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the required answer when an opponent cites a conflicting Companion saying to counter a proof based on a Companion's saying?
A) The claimant must immediately abandon his proof.
B) The claimant must discuss the opposing narration in a way that nullifies it.
C) The claimant must cite another, more authoritative Companion.
D) The claimant must prove that the opponents are not reliable.

Key Takeaway
In jadal, objecting by citing Companion disagreement requires the original debater to actively nullify the opposing narration, not merely acknowledge the disagreement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify an example from Islamic jurisprudence where two Companions differed on a ruling. Construct a dialectical exchange: the claimant uses one Companion's saying; the opponent objects by citing another Companion's saying. Then write the required answer that nullifies the opposing narration.
?
Analyze the second example in the passage: explain how the majority's answer (showing Umar's retraction) effectively nullifies the Maliki objection. Why is retraction a valid form of nullification?
